<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17461918384893851173">Top ten New York Times bestselling author J.A. Jance brings us another mesmerizing thriller featuring Arizona Sheriff Joanna Brady as she searches for the brutal killer of a young girl.<br /><br />Brianna "Bree" O'Brien never returned from Skeleton Canyon. Someone brutally murdered the pretty, popular teenager who had stolen away under cover of darkness to rendezvous with her boyfrien</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17461918384893851173">Top ten New York Times bestselling author J.A. Jance brings us another mesmerizing thriller featuring Arizona Sheriff Joanna Brady as she searches for the brutal killer of a young girl.<br /><br />Brianna "Bree" O'Brien never returned from Skeleton Canyon. Someone brutally murdered the pretty, popular teenager who had stolen away under cover of darkness to rendezvous with her boyfriend. Perhaps youthful rage, jealousy and savage passion cost young Bree her life. Or maybe she stumbled onto something too dangerous to know. Sheriff Joanna Brady of Cochise County knows only too well the pain of losing a loved one to violence. But she is disturbed by the O'Brien's insistence that Bree's boyfriend is responsible for their daughter's slaying. Joanna senses there are words not being spoken, and dark mysteries locked behind doors of the sprawling O'Brien family compound. But it is the strange disappearance of a good friend that is pulling Sheriff Brady ever closer to the lethal nest of lies, greed and secrets hiding in a desolate corner of the Arizona desert - where the next blood that feeds the parched, cracked earth could be her own.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17461918384893851173">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_93246796">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93246796" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2288360-ladycalico" class="left imgcol" title="LadyCalico"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1241539428p2/2288360.jpg" alt="LadyCalico" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/93246796?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 10, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2288360-ladycalico" class="user" title="LadyCalico">LadyCalico</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer93246796">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2684311359464308671">This is one of those books that make me wish Goodreads had a 3.5 rating. I liked this book more than the books I rated 3-stars, but not as much as the others I rated 4-stars. The story gripped me in the beginning and in the ending, but lost me somewhere in the middle, where the writing, relationships, and banter seemed to lose some of their depth and realism. On the other hand, I really, really liked the protagonist who seems more like a real person than the stereotypes of females that I often f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2684311359464308671">This is one of those books that make me wish Goodreads had a 3.5 rating. I liked this book more than the books I rated 3-stars, but not as much as the others I rated 4-stars. The story gripped me in the beginning and in the ending, but lost me somewhere in the middle, where the writing, relationships, and banter seemed to lose some of their depth and realism. On the other hand, I really, really liked the protagonist who seems more like a real person than the stereotypes of females that I often find in books written by women authors--so girlie that they are more like transvestites than real women with real lives. I found JoAnna very real and very sympathetic. I could relate heart and soul to the "sandwich" theme with her being at the stage of life when you have to shunt your own needs and wants to fourth place while you are busy doing a fancy tap dance trying to deal with both a young child and a difficult parent while also trying to keep food on the table--and keep the table--that's real life for most divorced, widowed, or single women--not worries about whether your Manolo's or Jimmy Choos go better with your Glock.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2684311359464308671">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_35853174">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35853174" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/797803-julianne" class="left imgcol" title="Julianne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1231180744p2/797803.jpg" alt="Julianne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/35853174?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 21, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/797803-julianne" class="user" title="Julianne">Julianne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer35853174">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12955385236585163855">This is Book #5 of the Joanna Brady Mystery Series. Wonderful! It starts out at a high school football game and ends up with murder and mayhem. In between you have Romeo and Juliet, nuns, smugglers, wild parrots, an abandoned cemetery, a search for Wedgewood China, Girl Scout camp, flash floods, people who elope, racism, at least three drunks, a flying bra, javelina tracks, a helicopter rescue and the fireworks on the Fourth of July. <br /><br />Which is better in the hot summer of Southern Arizona, a Crown</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12955385236585163855">This is Book #5 of the Joanna Brady Mystery Series. Wonderful! It starts out at a high school football game and ends up with murder and mayhem. In between you have Romeo and Juliet, nuns, smugglers, wild parrots, an abandoned cemetery, a search for Wedgewood China, Girl Scout camp, flash floods, people who elope, racism, at least three drunks, a flying bra, javelina tracks, a helicopter rescue and the fireworks on the Fourth of July. <br /><br />Which is better in the hot summer of Southern Arizona, a Crown Victoria with air conditioning or an Eagle SUV without? Well, it depends....are the washes running? If so, then you'd best get in the Hummer! This book takes us from Mount Lemmon to Bisbee to Peoria to the Mexican border. And in charge of it all is Joanna Brady, the sheriff of Cochise County. What a woman! In one day she rides a horse in the parade, hosts a wedding at her ranch in the afternoon and presides over the fireworks show that evening. And she does it all with grace, with authority and a gentle sense of humor. I recommend this book and this entire series to anyone who wants to have a wild adventure in reading!<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12955385236585163855">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1039941490">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16915867794493130653">This was the best of the series so far. Joanna has matured as a politician and a sheriff. The story is woven together well. Conflicts between the whites and people of Mexican descent are one of the focuses of this story as are the hopes and dreams parents have for their children and the children's needs to be independent of those dreams.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3571393142530963288">Brianna "Bree" O'Brien never returned from Skeleton Canyon. Someone brutally murdered the pretty, popular teenager who had stolen away under cover of darkness to rendezvous with her boyfriend. Perhaps youthful rage, jealousy and savage passion cost young Bree her life. Or maybe she stumbled onto something too dangerous to know. Sheriff Joanna Brady of Cochise County knows only too well the pain of losing a loved one to violence. But she is disturbed by the O'Brien's insistence that Bree's boyfri</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3571393142530963288">Brianna "Bree" O'Brien never returned from Skeleton Canyon. Someone brutally murdered the pretty, popular teenager who had stolen away under cover of darkness to rendezvous with her boyfriend. Perhaps youthful rage, jealousy and savage passion cost young Bree her life. Or maybe she stumbled onto something too dangerous to know. Sheriff Joanna Brady of Cochise County knows only too well the pain of losing a loved one to violence. But she is disturbed by the O'Brien's insistence that Bree's boyfriend is responsible for their daughter's slaying. Joanna senses there are words not being spoken, and dark mysteries locked behind doors of the sprawling O'Brien family compound. But it is the strange disappearance of a good friend that is pulling Sheriff Brady ever closer to the lethal nest of lies, greed and secrets hiding in a desolate corner of the Arizona desert - where the next blood that feeds the parched, cracked earth could be her own.<br />Bree is not murdered by her boyfriend, but by a cartel that want to use the O'Brien's land to smuggle freon, now illegal in the states passing through their land. She's in the wrong place at the wrong time.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_917721570">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/917721570" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4775358-bookmom" class="left imgcol" title="Bookmom"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Bookmom" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/917721570?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 22, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4775358-bookmom" class="user" title="Bookmom">Bookmom</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer917721570">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14031293773131829631">With this series we’re sometimes told right up front who the bad guy is, name and all. Other times we’re given some insight into the murderer, but don’t know who they are until much later. With this story we’re kept in the dark about the who and why until quite far into the book when looking into the murder of a teenager who’d gone missing.<br /><br />On the home front, both Joanna and Jenny are dealing with Andy’s death a lot better. It’s at least 9 months since his death. Jenny is especially doing well si</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14031293773131829631">With this series we’re sometimes told right up front who the bad guy is, name and all. Other times we’re given some insight into the murderer, but don’t know who they are until much later. With this story we’re kept in the dark about the who and why until quite far into the book when looking into the murder of a teenager who’d gone missing.<br /><br />On the home front, both Joanna and Jenny are dealing with Andy’s death a lot better. It’s at least 9 months since his death. Jenny is especially doing well since getting Kiddo, the horse from the prior book. But Jenny gets taken to Girl Scout Camp for a couple of weeks and Joanna is definitely having an empty-nest-syndrome feeling going on. So it’s a good thing that work is keeping her busy. And speaking of work, things are going better on that front as she’s earned the respect of those who work closest with her. Of course not everyone is on the Sheriff Joanna Brady bandwagon; the first female sheriff in AZ.<br /><br />As like the earlier books in the series, Joanna pulls together the mystery from conversations with many people instead of through interrogation, and I love that aspect of the books. People aren’t always comfortable talking with her, but she doesn’t grill them, making a huge difference. <br /><br />We’ve got a mystery, scenery, drama, surprises, and a few scenes that will make you feel good. You’ve heard about how dangerous a sudden rainstorm can be in the desert? We learn why. Another aspect of the series I’m enjoying is the vivid description of the terrain and wildlife of the area.<br /><br />We’re constantly learning more about the secondary characters and this one is no exception. For some it’s like reading about old friends.<br /><br />These books could easily be read as stand-alones. There is enough back filler provided without drowning the story in them.<br /><br />Read from a library book.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14031293773131829631">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15128735316831224251">Hey, this time ethnic slurs were only used by people who were confirmed racists and also bad guys! And the good guy characters are appalled by the racism exhibited by the bad guys (one of whom ends up seeing the error of his ways and deciding being a racist, that's no good), and Joanna at one point corrects a good guy character's annoyance about Spanish words -- when she corrects his pronunciation of one (he</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15128735316831224251">Hey, this time ethnic slurs were only used by people who were confirmed racists and also bad guys! (And once by a Mexican character in a joke, in a usage I think qualifies as reclaiming.) And the good guy characters are appalled by the racism exhibited by the bad guys (one of whom ends up seeing the error of his ways and deciding being a racist, that's no good), and Joanna at one point corrects a good guy character's annoyance about Spanish words -- when she corrects his pronunciation of one (he is a transplanted Midwesterner), he grumps about what happened to good old English, and she responds, "You mean like Minnesota? Or Illinois?"<br /><br />So, loads better than previous books. Good work on that front.</span>

My husband enjoyed reading this as he grew up in the area and attended Douglas AZ high school, who was and still is Bisbee's greatest rival. Since the main plot revolves around a cheerleaders murder, it would especially appeal to those that know the area or could relate to those times when relationships between whites and hispanics (especially in border towns) was so frowned on.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer969170428">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8829307401342673745">This is another authors that I have been steadily reading for a while now. I wasn't completely sold with this book though. When I grab a mystery I want something that leaves me wondering who did it. I want to flip the pages rapidly trying to get to the end to discover the answer. Unfortunately, this book was lacking that aspect. Don't get me wrong, it wasn't a horrible book. It was an quick, enjoyable book, but it lacked the depth I was hoping to find. <br /><br />Joanna Brady is searching for the killer of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8829307401342673745">This is another authors that I have been steadily reading for a while now. I wasn't completely sold with this book though. When I grab a mystery I want something that leaves me wondering who did it. I want to flip the pages rapidly trying to get to the end to discover the answer. Unfortunately, this book was lacking that aspect. Don't get me wrong, it wasn't a horrible book. It was an quick, enjoyable book, but it lacked the depth I was hoping to find. <br /><br />Joanna Brady is searching for the killer of Bri O'Brien, a bright young girl whose body is found in Skeleton Canyon. Along the way she discovers a group smuggling in Freon. <br /><br />To be perfectly honest that is all that really happens in this book. I think the major problem, for me, is the multiple storylines. The book is spread too thin and it causes the story to loose focus at times. You have Angie dating the birdman, a kidnapping, a chase, the murder of a girl, the dysfunctional parents of the murdered girl, the back story of the mother of the girl, the back story of the father of the girl, and the marriage of Joanna Brady's mother. It was just too much and took away from the book in the end. Not only that but it felt as though some of the side stories didn't add up to anything by the end of the book, which is annoying to say the least. <br /><br />Not a bad read, but nothing new or special. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8829307401342673745">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Now it was time for the uniformed yell squads of both schools to travel to opposite sides of the field. <span id="freeTextContainer12829877987202479403">Good series set in the country area where my daughter, Jana, lives. I like the characterization and the ideals. The mysteries are good puzzles, realistic, with a hint of jeopardy and adventure. They are for mature readers, with some language and frankness about feelings and sexuality (very tasteful and not usually explicit). In this novel, Joanna Brady must solve the murder of a young girl who goes to meet her boyfriend secretly because her parents object because he's Mexican. </span>

      <a href="/user/show/7413967-karen" class="user" title="Karen">Karen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer884681942">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17346169782595919900">I haven't read a book from Jance for a while, but this one reminded me why I had liked her books. Jance's protagonist is a female sherriff from Arizona. I like that this character, Joanna, is very well 'fleshed out' by the author. You can see the character throughout the book, which I find necessary to enjoy the book. Joanna is still recovering from the loss of her husband, and trying to make a life for herself and her daughter. Joanna is a strong woman, but the case she is thrown into involves</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17346169782595919900">I haven't read a book from Jance for a while, but this one reminded me why I had liked her books. Jance's protagonist is a female sherriff from Arizona. I like that this character, Joanna, is very well 'fleshed out' by the author. You can see the character throughout the book, which I find necessary to enjoy the book. Joanna is still recovering from the loss of her husband, and trying to make a life for herself and her daughter. Joanna is a strong woman, but the case she is thrown into involves an 18-year old girl who has been horribly murdered. This girl had secrets, and so do her parents...and trying to find what is true and what actually happened to this girl takes a lot of effort on Joanna's part. She also has to deal with some problems as concerns her deputies, and where the crime scene is (as well as problems with a friend and acquaintance getting mixed up with some criminal activity by accident), ends up putting Joanna and her deputies at risk due to flash flooding that is often seen with rainstorms in the ARizona desert. <br /><br />Jance writes well, and her books have a lot of good plotting, and are very descriptive. I love reading her 'color' writing on the Arizona that I'm familiar with. Makes me miss being there.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17346169782595919900">...more</a>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14744053198046764654">#5 in the Joanna Brady series. Joanna is a Sheriff in Cochise County, AZ; she was elected to the position after her husband of 10 years was shot to death while a front runner in the election. Joanna has become a respected and competent Sheriff and the books in this series are invariable good, quick reads as she progresses in her job and handles her family life as well.<br /><br />Joanna Brady is called to investigate the disappearance of 18 year old Bree O'Brien. With no evidence of kidnapping, Brady refuses to call in the FBI. In fact Bree has run off for a weekend rendezvous with her Latino boyfriend. The boyfriend is delayed, Bree is murdered and the plot becomes involved with Freon smugglers. Joanna's mother is secretly married. Butch visits.</span>

ANY PERSONAL NOTATIONS ARE FOR MY RECOLLECTION ONLY<br /><br />3.5 stars<br />With this series we’re sometimes told right up front who the bad guy is, name and all. Other times we’re given some insight into the murderer, but don’t know who they are until much later. With this story we’re kept in the dark about the who and why until quite far into the book when looking into the murd</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15147630910994092038">THIS SUMMARY/REVIEW WAS COPIED FROM OTHER SOURCES AND IS USED ONLY AS A REMINDER OF WHAT THE BOOK WAS ABOUT FOR MY PERSONAL INTEREST. ANY PERSONAL NOTATIONS ARE FOR MY RECOLLECTION ONLY<br /><br />3.5 stars<br />With this series we’re sometimes told right up front who the bad guy is, name and all. Other times we’re given some insight into the murderer, but don’t know who they are until much later. With this story we’re kept in the dark about the who and why until quite far into the book when looking into the murder of a teenager who’d gone missing.<br /><br />On the home front, both Joanna and Jenny are dealing with Andy’s death a lot better. It’s at least 9 months since his death. Jenny is especially doing well since getting Kiddo, the horse from the prior book. But Jenny gets taken to Girl Scout Camp for a couple of weeks and Joanna is definitely having an empty-nest-syndrome feeling going on. So it’s a good thing that work is keeping her busy. And speaking of work, things are going better on that front as she’s earned the respect of those who work closest with her. Of course not everyone is on the Sheriff Joanna Brady bandwagon; the first female sheriff in AZ.<br /><br />As like the earlier books in the series, Joanna pulls together the mystery from conversations with many people instead of through interrogation, and I love that aspect of the books. People aren’t always comfortable talking with her, but she doesn’t grill them, making a huge difference. <br /><br />We’ve got a mystery, scenery, drama, surprises, and a few scenes that will make you feel good. You’ve heard about how dangerous a sudden rainstorm can be in the desert? We learn why. Another aspect of the series I’m enjoying is the vivid description of the terrain and wildlife of the area.<br /><br />**************<br /><br /><br />Nov 30, 2011 Elise M. rated it 4 of 5 stars · review of another edition <br /><br /><br /><br /> Skeleton Canyon is a book in the Joanna Brady series. Ms. Brady is Sheriff of Cochise County, based in Bisbee, Arizona, but with plenty of journeys to the Tucson area. It's fun to read a book and know the places that are part of the story. As the story opens, Joanna Brady is driving her daughter to the Girl Scout camp on Mount Lemmon. That's not too far from my house.<br /><br />Meanwhile, a young girl back in Cochise County tells her parents that she's going to spend the weekend with a girlfriend in New Mexico, but is really having a rendezvous with her boyfriend in the Peloncillo Mountains. The secrecy is made necessary because Nacio, the boyfriend, is of Mexican heritage and her parents, particularly her father, are biased against Mexicans. Unfortunately, Nacio has to work and can't join her right away, so she goes up by herself to wait for him.<br /><br />When she hears a car coming up the mountain, she assumes it is Nacio coming to join her. It isn't. She is murdered by the intruder and it's Joanna Brady's duty to find her killer. Of course, there are other complications.<br /><br />This is a very enjoyable mystery. It has all the elements of a well put together plot. But what I really liked was the fact that there's a believable cast of characters. One of these is a woman minister. People in this novel go to church, call on the minister for help, and even offer brief prayers when the occasion calls for it. There's tension between Joanna and her mother, but also love. There's the friend with the shady past who's really a decent person. We root for her as she tries to turn her life around and gets disappointed.<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer509463810">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7703039684962159904">I decided several months ago to read the Joanna Brady series from start to finish. I had read several of the books years ago and then stopped. I am now beginning to think I know the reason I quit reading the series the first time around. It's not that the books are bad per se; they are just a bit too repetitive. As in the prior four books, there is a murder that Joanna is trying to solve while also dealing with home related issues as well. I don't have a problem with that basic format but I feel</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7703039684962159904">I decided several months ago to read the Joanna Brady series from start to finish. I had read several of the books years ago and then stopped. I am now beginning to think I know the reason I quit reading the series the first time around. It's not that the books are bad per se; they are just a bit too repetitive. As in the prior four books, there is a murder that Joanna is trying to solve while also dealing with home related issues as well. I don't have a problem with that basic format but I feel as if the character growth should be increasing with each new book in the series. Unfortunately, that isn't happening all that much. There is a surprising event that occurs related to Joanna's mother, Eleanor, which was interesting but beyond that the reader doesn't learn much more about the characters that wasn't already known from prior books. <br /><br />While this book certainly wasn't a page turner for me, I am not quite ready to give up the series for a second time. Hopefully the next installment will be more promising. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7703039684962159904">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5581636937572218874">Skeleton Canyon is a book in the Joanna Brady series. Ms. Brady is Sheriff of Cochise County, based in Bisbee, Arizona, but with plenty of journeys to the Tucson area. It's fun to read a book and know the places that are part of the story. As the story opens, Joanna Brady is driving her daughter to the Girl Scout camp on Mount Lemmon. That's not too far from my house.<br /><br />Meanwhile, a young girl back in Cochise County tells her parents that she's going to spend the weekend with a girlfriend in New Me</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5581636937572218874">Skeleton Canyon is a book in the Joanna Brady series. Ms. Brady is Sheriff of Cochise County, based in Bisbee, Arizona, but with plenty of journeys to the Tucson area. It's fun to read a book and know the places that are part of the story. As the story opens, Joanna Brady is driving her daughter to the Girl Scout camp on Mount Lemmon. That's not too far from my house.<br /><br />Meanwhile, a young girl back in Cochise County tells her parents that she's going to spend the weekend with a girlfriend in New Mexico, but is really having a rendezvous with her boyfriend in the Peloncillo Mountains. The secrecy is made necessary because Nacio, the boyfriend, is of Mexican heritage and her parents, particularly her father, are biased against Mexicans. Unfortunately, Nacio has to work and can't join her right away, so she goes up by herself to wait for him.<br /><br />When she hears a car coming up the mountain, she assumes it is Nacio coming to join her. It isn't. She is murdered by the intruder and it's Joanna Brady's duty to find her killer. Of course, there are other complications.<br /><br />This is a very enjoyable mystery. It has all the elements of a well put together plot. But what I really liked was the fact that there's a believable cast of characters. One of these is a woman minister. People in this novel go to church, call on the minister for help, and even offer brief prayers when the occasion calls for it. There's tension between Joanna and her mother, but also love. There's the friend with the shady past who's really a decent person. We root for her as she tries to turn her life around and gets disappointed.<br /><br />I own several of J.A. Jance's novels. I've been to a couple of her book signings here in Tucson. But somehow this is the first book that I've pulled off my To Be Read pile (or TBR shelf on my nook). This is definitely a series I want to read in total.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer188128329">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13296227719022575699">This is the 5th book in the Joanna Brady series, and follows the same pattern as the rest of the series: Joanna deals with personal issues while solving a murder (or several). While there is nothing really new in the way the story is presented, the execution is good. We meet another new denizen of the Bisbee area, Dennis Hacker, who becomes involved with Angie (the ex-prostitute) in a budding romance. We learn that Joanna's mother has eloped without telling Joanna - and that the new husband is n</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13296227719022575699">This is the 5th book in the Joanna Brady series, and follows the same pattern as the rest of the series: Joanna deals with personal issues while solving a murder (or several). While there is nothing really new in the way the story is presented, the execution is good. We meet another new denizen of the Bisbee area, Dennis Hacker, who becomes involved with Angie (the ex-prostitute) in a budding romance. We learn that Joanna's mother has eloped without telling Joanna - and that the new husband is none other than the town Medical Examiner. All in all, the murders serve the same purpose as in all of the Brady books - to advance the story of Joanna's personal life and her interactions with the community. And, in the end, that makes for an interesting story based on people, more than events. Worth the read.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer12487117611640848521">Bree O'Brien had plans to meet her boyfriend for a weekend camping trip. Her boyfriend had to work Friday night and Saturday morning so Bree decided to go camping alone and wait on him. She is murdered before he can get there. Sheriff Joanna Brady of Cochise County and her deputies investigate the crime.<br /><br />This is the fifth book in the Joanna Brady series. I have not read any of the others but this one was very good and can be read alone.</span>

          </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12020146161207116348"><strong>Great read</strong><br /><br />I have enjoyed many of J. A. Janice books. This is the first e-book. I gave it 4 stars because I found the typography broke my train of thought. Also, they hyphenated words were used improperly. <br />I love the setting. of Bisbee as over the years I've visited During many of it's incarnations. We thought of moving there but. at that time it had no hospital and even fewer homes to buy. I was there in 2010 and visited the many little boutique shops. These stories are artfully woven and the threads of this mystery wind through relationships, guilt and the stress amongst some Anglos and Hispanics. A story of young love and love lost. I recommend this book.<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('44SQ+CYNd2ECyh/tDEc+DzvP/ngg/MeyXcnOZtDdp86GUK8r1N9jm44Sa1ZyJti9cjg9YWkhgBg3wMv0HEhRiw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Y4BN0mc2RFIX3rVh3VyycmZ1wNrT4X6xzXmXeCzia8YGVHIBleRQqJsGwdqjPVTAL4IDw5o8ORuncJLq4Hedgw==')})
  }

Martha &amp;quot;Marty&amp;quot; Nickerson is a lawyer who truly loves her job. As an assistant D.A. for Massachusetts\'s Barnstable County, which includes all the small towns on Cape Cod, she speaks for the victims of crime and their families, and sees the system as a means for doing right.\n\nThe case of Manuel Rodriguez is a prime example. Rodriguez is accused of brutally murdering a college student, a kind young man who had a bright future. Marty has worked hard on this case; as the mother of a teenage son, she identifies with the murdered boy\'s grieving parents. Her case against Rodriguez is so solid that even public defender Harry Madigan -- the champion of the Cape\'s underdogs -- expects a conviction. And, on Memorial Day, exactly a year after the crime, the verdict comes in: guilty as charged. Justice prevails.\n\nThen, with Rodriguez behind bars, another body turns up in disturbingly similar circumstances. Did Marty and her colleagues target the wrong man? Her supervisor -- Geraldine Schilling, who aspires to be the county\'s first female D.A. -- refuses to reopen such a high-profile case. Why should she? The prosecutors played by the rules and won big. But Marty fears that the real killer will strike again.\n\nWith her career on the line and lives at stake, Marty must rely on her own moral compass, legal savvy, and gut instinct as she matches wits with a twisted killer. The system itself is on trial as Marty tries to serve Justice, not merely the Law.\n\nOnly an author with years of courtroom experience could add such riveting authenticity to a novel thatasks important questions and provides surprising answers.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3453636.J_A_Jance">About J.A. Jance</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3453636.J_A_Jance"><img alt="3453636" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1285182279p2/3453636.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer2361847034977593092">Judith Ann Jance is the top 10 New York Times bestselling author of the Joanna Brady series; the J. P. Beaumont series; three interrelated thrillers featuring the Walker family; and Edge of Evil, the first in a series featuring Ali Reynolds. Born in South Dakota and brought up in Bisbee, Arizona, Jance lives with her husband in Seattle, Washington, and Tucson, Arizona.<br /><br /><strong>Series:</strong><br />* <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/series/41261-j-p-beaumont">J.P. Beaumont</a><br />* <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/series/40431-joanna-brady">Joann</a></span>

In the suffocating stillness of an airless trailer, a woman is lying dead, a bullet hole in her chest. Why someone would murder a harmless loner with a soft spot for strays is only one of the questions nagging at the local police; another is why the killer used an eighty-five-year-old bullet, fired from the same weapon that slaughtered two other women who were discovered bound, naked, and gruesomely posed on the remote edge of a rancher?s land. The slayings are as oppressive as the blistering heat for Sheriff Joanna Brady, who must shoulder the added double burden of a brutal re-election campaign and major developments on the home front. With more on her plate suddenly than many big city law officers have to contend with, she must put marital distractions and an opponent?s dirty tricks in the background and deal with the terrifying reality that now threatens everyone in her jurisdiction: a serial killer in their midst.
